**Previously updated:** May 15, 2026 (**Eightieth Claude Code session — W#2 P-12 SHIPPED at code level on `workflow-2-competition-scraping` — extension 401-retry / silent-refresh analog to P-1, per ROADMAP Active Tools W#2 row (a.14).** Launch-prompt task was: ship P-12 mirroring P-1's `makeAuthFetch` shape; check whether W#2 branch needs `origin/main` merged in BEFORE adding new commits (per CORRECTIONS_LOG 2026-05-10-c entry #1 PROCESS finding). `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/api-client.ts` `authedFetch` refactored to a factory `makeAuthedFetch({ supabase, fetchFn })` mirroring P-1's `makeAuthFetch` in `src/lib/authFetch.ts`. On 401, the wrapper calls `supabase.auth.refreshSession()` once and retries with the new access token; on refresh failure, returns the original 401 unchanged so the caller's existing `PlosApiError(401)` error path is preserved. Production export wraps `fetch` in an arrow `(u, i) => fetch(u, i)` to preserve the window receiver — applying the P-17 lesson from the 2026-05-12 hotfix `08f10e5` proactively. Pre-fetch no-token check still throws `PlosApiError(401, "Not signed in")`; `mapFetchTransportError` wraps BOTH the first attempt AND the retry (TypeError → `PlosApiError(0, "Network unreachable")` semantics survive across the silent-refresh path). **Tests added:** `api-client.test.ts` extended with 9 new tests mirroring `src/lib/authFetch.test.ts`'s 7-test pattern plus 2 extension-specific cases (TypeError on first attempt; TypeError on retry after successful refresh). Test count 252 → 261 (+9). **Verification scoreboard:** 261/261 ext tests pass; ext `tsc --noEmit` clean (after adding `!` non-null assertions on `calls[N]` array accesses — extension tsconfig has `noUncheckedIndexedAccess: true` which web tsconfig doesn't); `wxt build` clean (6 artifacts at 676K — baseline parity). **Branch state at session start:** W#2 was 4 commits behind `origin/main` (P-17 + Rule 27 + platform-UI fix-pair + 2026-05-12-b deploy doc-batch); director picked merge over rebase via Rule 14f forced-picker; `git merge origin/main` FAST-FORWARDED cleanly (zero conflicts) because main's 2026-05-12-b deploy session had already absorbed W#2's prior 2026-05-12 doc-batch commit `23375bd`. **First session to apply CORRECTIONS_LOG 2026-05-10-c entry #1 protocol** (pull-main-into-feature-branch-at-session-start) — worked as designed; no rebase complications; no force-push needed. **Multi-Workflow per Rule 25:** session stayed on `workflow-2-competition-scraping` end-to-end; no W#1 row change; schema-change-in-flight stays "No"; no cross-workflow doc edits. **TaskList sweep per Rule 26:** 6 main session tasks tracked + all completed; **zero `DEFERRED:` items captured this session** (all P-12 in-scope work shipped; no out-of-scope items surfaced). **Two commits this session:** code+tests commit `414efe6` on `workflow-2-competition-scraping`; end-of-session doc batch on same branch. Removing the cap auto-resolved the backlog's recommended (e) dedupe warning + (f) skip-if-unchanged measurement — no cap → no warning → no `document.body.textContent.length` re-measure overhead. 9 new tests added to `highlight-terms.test.ts` for `processInChunks`. **Director picked Option A "Proceed with all three fixes today P-2 → P-10 → P-9 (Recommended)"** at session start via Rule 14f forced-picker, despite ROADMAP's Active Tools W#2 row Next Session list having `(a.4)` deploy as RECOMMENDED NEXT — Claude surfaced the ordering trade-off transparently in the drift check before the picker fired. **Verification scoreboard:** ext compile clean; ext tests **220/220** pass (was 205/205 — +6 P-2 + +9 P-9 processInChunks); ext build clean (**638.82 KB total**); ext lint clean (npx eslint exit 0; "Pages directory" informational message from inherited Next eslint plugin not a lint error); root tsc clean; root build clean (**50 routes** exact baseline parity — no new routes); root tests **393/393** pass exact baseline parity; root lint **52 problems (13e/39w)** exact baseline parity. **Browser verification: NOT YET — code lives on `workflow-2-competition-scraping` only; not on main; vklf.com runs prior code.** Combined with session #7's P-3 narrowed work (commit `16d4351`), the W#2-vs-main deploy gap now covers FOUR polish items (P-2 + P-3 narrowed + P-9 + P-10) plus session #7's schema addition; next deploy session (item (a.4) in Active Tools row) will browser-verify all four together. **Multi-workflow per Rule 25:** pull-rebase clean at session start; W#1 row untouched per Rule 3 ownership; schema-change-in-flight stayed "No" entire session — none of P-2/P-9/P-10 touched `prisma/schema.prisma`. **TaskList sweep at end-of-session per Rule 26:** 5 tasks tracked + completed; **zero `DEFERRED:` items at any point.** Two commits: code (this session's three fixes) + end-of-session doc-batch (this commit). new `scheduleDetailOverlayCheck()` 150ms-debounced cancellable timer ensures only the final URL gets a banner check after pushState bursts; MutationObserver-based SPA URL change detection via new `lastObservedUrl` closure variable — checks `location.href !== lastObservedUrl` inside the existing 250ms-debounced rescan callback and triggers the overlay-check debouncer if changed. **Critical technical wrinkle that drove the design:** Chrome content scripts run in an **isolated world** with their own `window.history`, so patching `pushState` in content-script context does NOT intercept host-page React Router calls (Walmart, etc.) — the MutationObserver is the cross-context-safe signal since SPA navigation always causes immediate DOM mutation paired with a URL change. Initial-load detail-overlay check at orchestrator startup also routes through the debouncer — gives Walmart's React time to settle URL after content-script load. Cleanup function clears any pending overlay-check + rescan timers on teardown. Per existing extension test convention (DOM-touching code verified end-to-end in browser, only pure logic unit-tested), no new unit tests added for these orchestrator changes — relies on next waypoint walkthrough for browser verification across Amazon + Ebay + Etsy + Walmart. **(P-9) `MAX_BODY_TEXT_LEN_BYTES` constant + `pageTooLarge()` function REMOVED entirely.** Replaced with chunked/incremental highlight pass via `requestIdleCallback`. New exported `processInChunks<T>(items, processItem, options)` generic chunk-and-yield helper (default chunk size 500 nodes ≈ 10-15ms/chunk on typical pages with ~25μs/text-node wrap; pluggable `yieldFn` for unit testing without browser idle-callback API; honors `CancellationSignal` between chunks — returns at next chunk boundary if `signal.cancelled` becomes true mid-pass). `applyHighlightsTo` is now async + chunked — collects text nodes upfront via TreeWalker (existing pattern; cheap synchronous DOM read), then processes them via `processInChunks`. Honors cancellation in BOTH the collect phase (between TreeWalker steps) and the wrap phase (between chunks). `startLiveHighlighting.refresh()` rewritten for last-wins cancellation — new `activeApplySignal: CancellationSignal | null` closure variable tracks in-flight pass; each new `refresh()` cancels the previous (sets `signal.cancelled = true`) before starting fresh; wrapped in try/finally so the active-signal slot is cleared on completion or cancellation; `destroy()` also cancels in-flight passes for clean teardown. MutationObserver debounce stays at 250ms in orchestrator.ts — cancellation-on-new-refresh handles rapid re-fire churn cleanly: rapid SPA mutations on Walmart will cancel + restart refreshes, with the latest DOM-state always becoming the eventual visible state. **Removing the cap auto-resolved the backlog's recommended (e) dedupe warning + (f) skip-if-unchanged measurement** — no cap → no warning to dedupe → no expensive `document.body.textContent.length` re-measure overhead. 9 new tests added to `extensions/competition-scraping/src/lib/content-script/highlight-terms.test.ts` for `processInChunks` (chunk boundaries / no yield within chunks / no trailing yield / empty input / signal cancellation mid-pass / signal cancellation before first item / default chunkSize / ordering invariant). **Verification scoreboard:** ext compile clean; DOC + LIVE-RUN session — no code changes — but a CONCLUSIVE EMPIRICAL FINDING.** Director executed item (a) of the prior STATE block's standing instructions: pool-tune-only investigation on Pro tier. **Three-step plan ran:** (i) Pro tier confirmed active in Supabase dashboard; (ii) Database → Configuration → Settings revealed compute size is **"Nano"** (smallest available — Pro plan unlocks the configurable knob but does NOT auto-bump compute), pool size at default **15** for Nano (Postgres `max_connections` fixed at **60** on Nano per dashboard's 80% warning when 60 attempted), bumped to **40** (67% of 60-cap with 13-point buffer below Supabase's 80% warning threshold; covers estimated 22-burst with 18 spare); (iii) small-batch test on Bursitis Test 2 batch 2 (resumed from 30/291 checkpoint at canvas 124). **Test outcome:** model + canvas-rebuild side clean ($0.320, 19 ops applied, 2 archived keywords correctly identified — Greg Hayes proper-name + Capsella bursa-pastoris botanical Latin; no quality regression); **post-rebuild UI refresh failed identically to 2026-05-04-c** with HTTP 500 on /canvas + /canvas/nodes; same `FATAL: Max client connections reached` in expanded Vercel logs. **CRITICAL FINDING from log expansion:** the 2026-05-04-c estimate of "~22 parallel PATCHes" was WRONG by a factor of ~2.5×: actual burst is **55-60+ parallel PATCH calls per batch** (counted: ~40 successful PATCH 200s + ~18 PATCH 500s in a 3-second window during tonight's batch 2 with 19 operations). Earlier 22 estimate was based on a Vercel view showing only failures (collapsed/filtered); tonight's expanded view shows the full burst. **Implication: pool tune at Nano compute is structurally insufficient.** Pool 40 absorbs ~40 of 58; pool 48 (max safe under 80% warning) ~10 short; pool 60 (100% of max_connections) at Supabase's instability line. **Per standing instructions, this triggers the pivot to the parallel-PATCH-burst reduction code-fix (ROADMAP item d).** The wall cannot be cleared by config at this compute tier; code-side reduction is structurally required. Three approaches: (i) client-side worker queue serializing the 55-60+ parallel PATCHes (~10-20 LOC, lowest risk, ZERO quality impact, ~3-6s slower per batch); (ii) bulk PATCH /keywords endpoint collapse (existing endpoint accepts arrays; needs audit; faster); (iii) atomic-batch-into-rebuild-transaction (largest refactor; ZERO quality impact; ELIMINATES P2025 race condition for free; most thorough). Per director's standing preference for most-thorough-and-reliable, approach (iii) is likely recommendation pending code review at next session start. **Bonus finding (BONUS in the "we got lucky to find it" sense — captured as separate MEDIUM ROADMAP entry):** one of the failed PATCHes (keyword 78c696c5) returned a DIFFERENT error type — `P2025 "No record was found for an update"` — NOT pool exhaustion. Likely a race condition where the canvas-rebuild $transaction archived a keyword while a parallel PATCH was still in-flight against it. Eliminated for free by code-fix approach (iii); not necessarily by approaches (i) or (ii). **Methodology improvement codified this session: HANDOFF_PROTOCOL.md Rule 26 NEW (2026-05-04-d) — Real-time deferred-items registry via TaskCreate** (formal Rule 14e-extension). Drafted mid-session after director's framing: *"We have a lot of sessions and our overall roadmap is long. Even small things being dropped like this can prove catastrophic. There should be a method to ensure nothing necessary gets ignored."* The slip that triggered codification: Claude said "I'll capture this as a sanity-check item in the deferred sweep too" without naming the destination doc — Rule 14e violation. Before today's fix, runLoop's outer catch retried the WHOLE batch with stale client state, producing two failure modes: visible (cyclic stableId references caught by applier guards — observed at Batch 15 attempt 2 in 2026-05-02-c) AND silent (per-(projectWorkflowId, stableId) upsert collisions silently overwriting attempt-1 content; no guard catches this). **(3) Option A from this session's design picker — recommended + chosen.** New pure helper `src/lib/post-rebuild-fetch-retry.ts` (~150 lines incl. extensive header comment) wraps the post-rebuild refresh in a 3-attempt retry loop (waits 2s, 5s); on persistent failure throws annotated `Error` carrying `_noRetry: true` AND `_postRebuildFetchFailed: true` plus self-explanatory user-facing message ("Canvas rebuild SUCCEEDED but UI refresh failed after 3 attempts. | 2026-04-30 | session_2026-04-30-b_scale-session-c-build (Claude Code) | Workflow #1 (Keyword Clustering / Auto-Analyze) — Scale Session C build (Tiered Canvas Serialization mechanism per `INPUT_CONTEXT_SCALING_DESIGN.md` §6) | Phase 1 — Admin-solo tooling — Workflow #1 architectural scaling, mechanism land | **Twenty-sixth Claude Code session — second build session of the day; option (a) from the prior STATE block. Lowercase + split on non-alphanumeric + drop stopwords + drop tokens shorter than 3 chars. ~30 LOC. Forgiving design (≥2-stem heuristic threshold) makes perfect stemming unnecessary; swap to full Porter or `natural` is a one-function change if validation later reveals poor recall. Autonomous detail per Rule 14d. **(2) `computeBatchRelevantSubtree(ctx)` (Cluster 3 locks).** For each canvas topic builds a stem set from (title + intent fingerprint + linked-keyword text). Aggregates per-keyword stem-overlap scores across the batch; thresholds at ≥2 stems (`BATCH_RELEVANCE_MIN_STEMS = 2`); promotes candidates' one-hop neighborhood (self + parent + siblings + children) to the result Set. Empty batch → empty subtree. ~80 LOC. Sub-millisecond on a 1,000-topic canvas. **(3) `decideTier(input)` (Cluster 2 locks).** Pure signal-based decider. Tier 0 force conditions (any of): in-batch-subtree / touched within recency window / stability < 7.0. Tier 2 eligibility (AND-rule): stability ≥ 7.0 AND deeply stale (>10 batches) AND not in subtree. Default Tier 1 (settled but not deep-stale). Constants exported: `STABILITY_TIER_THRESHOLD = 7.0`, `DEFAULT_RECENCY_WINDOW = 5`, `TIER_2_DEEP_STALE_THRESHOLD = 10`. ~25 LOC. Q9 (no ancestor force-promotion) honored by design — the function knows nothing about hierarchy. **(4) Touch tracker + helpers.** `TouchTracker = Map<stableId, lastTouchedBatchNum>`. `createTouchTracker`, `recordTouchesFromOps(tracker, ops, currentBatchNum, aliasResolutions)` walks the post-apply alias map and stamps every topic ref in every op body. `batchesSinceTouch` returns null when never touched else `current − last`. JSON-safe `serializeTouchTracker` (`Map → Record<string, number>`) + `deserializeTouchTracker` (inverse, tolerates null/undefined input). Conservative inclusion: every ref in every op stamps (reassign targets, parents, sister-link endpoints all included; ARCHIVE_KEYWORD touches nothing per spec). Q5 → C: no ancestor propagation. ~80 LOC. **(5) Tier 1 / Tier 2 row formatters + `formatTier1KeywordSummary`.** Tier 1 row: 6 columns (Stable ID, Title, Parent Stable ID, Stability Score, Intent Fingerprint, Keyword Summary). Tier 2 row: 3 columns (Stable ID, Title, Parent Stable ID). Keyword summary string per Cluster 1 Q3 lock: `'{N} keywords ({P}p + {S}s), top volume kw: "{text}" ({V})'`. Empty topic → `'0 keywords'`. Top-volume picked by volume desc, alphabetical tiebreaker; missing/non-numeric volumes sort as 0. `KeywordLite.volume` loosened to `number \| string \| undefined` to accept the ambient `Keyword` shape (string from import path; Int in Prisma) — formatter coerces. **(6) Tiered TSV builder.** Three sections delimited by `=== TIER 0 ===` / `=== TIER 1 ===` / `=== TIER 2 ===`; empty tiers omitted. Tier 0 reuses the V3 9-column layout via the refactored `buildFullTsv` helper. **Empty-fingerprint pin** per §4.2 last paragraph: topics with empty `intentFingerprint` cannot be safely demoted (Tier 1's load-bearing intent-equivalence signal would be missing) — serializer force-pins them to Tier 0 regardless of decider signals. | 2026-04-28 | session_2026-04-28_deeper-analysis-and-fix-design (Claude Code) | Platform / Workflow #1 (Keyword Clustering / Auto-Analyze) — deeper-analysis + fix-design session: diagnose canvas-blanking bug to root cause + characterize live Bursitis canvas quality issues + code reading on `useCanvas.ts` / `AutoAnalyze.tsx` / `auto-analyze-v3.ts` / `/canvas/rebuild` and `/canvas/nodes` API routes | Phase 1 — Admin-solo tooling — Workflow #1 deeper-analysis + fix design (no code changes; pure investigation) | **Twentieth Claude Code session — second session of the day; pure analysis + fix-design + ROADMAP-update session.** Per the standing instructions in the prior session's POST-2026-04-28-SCALE-SESSION-0-OUTCOME-C STATE block (option a). **Substantive outputs:** **(1) Canvas-blanking bug ROOT CAUSE DIAGNOSED.** `src/hooks/useCanvas.ts:75` — `setNodes(Array.isArray(nodesData) ? nodesData : [])` silently zeroes nodes whenever `/api/projects/[id]/canvas/nodes` GET returns a non-array body (e.g., a 5xx error JSON `{ error: 'Failed to fetch nodes' }`). Two design defects combine: `response.ok` never checked + non-array fallback is `[]` instead of `prev`. Most-likely 5xx trigger: connection-pool flake on the Supabase pgbouncer pooler under sustained run load (~2,500-3,800 transactions in ~3 hours of 151-batch run). Token signature math (~19,929 = cached system prompt + minimal user content with empty TSV) lines up exactly with the only code path that emits a header-only TSV; no competing hypothesis fits. **(2) SECOND HIGH-severity bug discovered.** Reconciliation-Pass Closure-Staleness at `AutoAnalyze.tsx:830` — `for (const kw of allKeywords)` reads the closure-frozen prop instead of the always-fresh `keywordsRef.current`. Violates the documented invariant at line 153 ("runLoop-reachable code must read via *Ref.current"). Regression of the 2026-04-18 stale-closure pattern in NEW code added in Session 3b (2026-04-25) — the line-153 invariant was already documented when the new code was written; the developer (Claude in Session 3b) didn't apply it. The same `doApplyV3` function correctly uses `keywordsRef.current` at line 656 — line 830 is the lone regression. **(3) Empirical math matches DB exactly.** 84 stuck Reshuffled keywords currently in DB, ALL 84 still on the canvas. The math: at run start the project carried ~84 AI-Sorted keywords from a prior in-flight run; the closure-frozen `allKeywords` showed those 84 as AI-Sorted forever; both blanking events flipped the SAME 84 to Reshuffled (closure said "AI-Sorted" + placedSet = 8 batch keywords); intervening healthy batches saw the same 84 in stale closure as still-AI-Sorted → no flip → no healing. **(4) Forensic confirmation in DB.** Live Bursitis canvas: 690 nodes, contiguous t-1..t-690, no nodes destroyed. 17 orphan-root + descendant nodes from the two blanking events, all created in two single transactions with identical timestamps (`2026-04-28T00:45:41.836Z` and `2026-04-28T03:16:35.901Z`). Titles match V3 prompt example funnel-stage roots almost verbatim (e.g., "What is bursitis?", "What can you do about bursitis?", "Something doesn't feel right — could it be bursitis?"). Confirms the model's behavior was correct for an empty canvas; the bug is upstream of the model. **(5) Status drift residuals.** 147 keywords AI-Sorted but actually OFF canvas (ghost AI-Sorted) + 85 keywords Unsorted/Reshuffled but actually ON canvas (silent placements) — partly attributable to the closure-staleness bug. **(6) Body-part ladder violation found at scale.** 95+ body-part-named topics (33 hip, 12 shoulder, 9 pes anserine, 8 elbow, 7 knee, 7 heel, 6 trochanteric, 4 iliopsoas, 4 ischial, etc.) live OUTSIDE their dedicated body-part anchor topics (`t-5 Hip bursitis`, `t-7 Shoulder bursitis`, etc.) under intent-organized branches like "What can you do about bursitis?" → "Treating hip bursitis". This is the V3 prompt Step 4b "under-placement" failure mode the prompt is supposed to prevent — but Step 4b is self-policed and the applier doesn't enforce it. Root cause: as canvas TSV grew past 100k tokens, model started shedding dimension-secondaries to manage output length. **This is the structural problem Scale Sessions B-E (Tiered Canvas Serialization + intentFingerprint) are designed to address.** **(7) Three duplicate-title pairs/triples confirmed.** "What is bursitis?" (`c3d2a80`) **Bug fix #1** — Test 1 surfaced applier rejecting ADD_TOPIC for root topics with `relationship: null`. Per PIVOT_DESIGN §1.1 + AUTO_ANALYZE_PROMPT_V3.md, relationship is "ignored for root" but the applier validated unconditionally as linear\|nested. (`1c44238`) **Diagnostic enrichment** — `/canvas/rebuild` route now returns the underlying Prisma error message in a `detail` field (truncated to 1KB); without this we couldn't diagnose Test 2 rebuild failures from server logs (director can't read them). (`6b70913`) **Bug fix #2** — Test 2 surfaced Prisma 6 P2025 "Record not found" on every `prisma.canvasNode.upsert`. Root cause: route used `where: { id, projectWorkflowId }` which is not a registered unique key in Prisma 6's WhereUniqueInput. Switch to the per-project composite unique `projectWorkflowId_stableId` introduced in Pivot Session B; backward-compatible — V2 callers don't send stableId, route falls back to `t-${n.id}` convention. (`43f773f`) **Bug fix #3 (root cause for Test 2 failure series)** — surfaced "Unique constraint failed on the fields: (`id`)". `CanvasNode.id` and `Pathway.id` are global `Int @id` primary keys but the application treats them as project-scoped via per-project `nextNodeId`/`nextPathwayId` counters in `CanvasState`. Test project's stored counter at 1 → V3 issued ids 1–7 → collision with Bursitis's 1–104. Switch `/canvas` GET autoheal aggregates from per-project to global max so the returned counter is past every existing id in the DB. Latent bug remains in `/canvas/nodes` POST (reads from DB without GET autoheal) — captured in ROADMAP for follow-up. (`d485cf9`) **Bug fix #4** — previous fix only kicked in when `CanvasState` row existed; for projects whose row was absent, GET returned `canvasState: null` and client fell back to `nextNodeId=1` → re-collision. Synthesize defaults with global-max-aware counters when row missing. (`d624556`) **Bug fix #5** — BATCH_REVIEW screen always showed "Topics: None" for V3 because `processBatchV3` returned `newTopics: []`; populate from parsed ADD_TOPIC operations after validation. **End-to-end validation on Bursitis (5+ batches across multiple runs, all succeeded after the fix series):** output tokens 15K–27K (V2 baseline 110,245 → ~5× reduction); cost per batch $0.27–$0.46 (V2 baseline $1.89 → ~4–7× reduction); wall-clock ~5–7 min (V2 baseline ~26 min → ~4× reduction); **zero keyword loss confirmed structurally — `Reconciliation: 0 off-canvas → Reshuffled` on every successful apply, validating the architectural pivot's main claim**. Rule 14f question framing on the push approval used yes/no/clarify/free-text pattern. **Commit:** docs-only — no code changes; `KEYWORD_CLUSTERING_ACTIVE.md` (new POST-VERIFICATION STATE block above POST-SESSION-3b STATE), `CORRECTIONS_LOG.md` (new 2026-04-25 verify entry — informational verification finding + low-severity planning miss + new architectural pattern), `ROADMAP.md` (Session 3b PUSH PENDING → PUSHED + verification block + new "Blank-canvas visual verification" polish item + Phase 1g-test follow-up REMAINING updated), `CHAT_REGISTRY.md` (this row), `DOCUMENT_MANIFEST.md` (timestamps + modified flags). **END-OF-SESSION ARCHITECTURAL INSIGHT (HIGH SEVERITY, captured in `CORRECTIONS_LOG.md` 2026-04-25 architectural-insight entry):** Director, post-handoff: *"Why did the cost and time sky rocket like this... we have been progressively fixing things and they are getting worse. Why are keywords being removed from topics that they belong in? Why are responses using so many tokens? Why is it taking so long?"* Forced honest re-examination. **Single root cause naming all three pain points:** the Auto-Analyze prompts ask the AI to **rebuild and re-emit the entire topics layout table** every batch (Initial Prompt: *"provide the complete updated Integrated Topics Layout Table"*; Primer rule 3: *"Never delete existing topics or keywords"*). The AI is being used as a **state-rebuilder** when it should be a **state-mutator**. Symptom mapping: (1) keyword loss = AI fails to re-emit prior placements as table grows (74 Reshuffled = exact match to Session 2 P3-F7 diagnosis); (2) cost-per-batch scales with canvas size (~105k of 110k output tokens are redundant re-emission); (3) wall-clock = output-token-rate-bottlenecked at ~50-80 tokens/sec on Sonnet 4.6. **Recent fixes are band-aids on this root cause** — reconciliation pass surfaces losses but doesn't prevent them; salvage is recovery not prevention; HC4/HC5/proposed-HC6 are detection only; stable topic IDs / Changes Ledger exist because rename detection in a full-table-rewrite is hard. **The fix:** change the AI's output contract from "complete updated TSV table" to "list of operations" (`ADD_TOPIC`, `RENAME_TOPIC`, `MOVE_TOPIC`, `MERGE_TOPICS`, `SPLIT_TOPIC`, `DELETE_TOPIC`, `ADD_KEYWORD`, `MOVE_KEYWORD`, `REMOVE_KEYWORD`, `ADD_SISTER_LINK`, `REMOVE_SISTER_LINK`). Tool — deterministic code, not AI — applies operations to existing canvas. Validation runs on applied result. **Direct consequences of pivot:** output drops 100k+ → <1k tokens (cost drops 99%+; wall-clock drops to <1 min); keywords cannot silently disappear (AI cannot drop a keyword without explicit operation); reconciliation pass / Reshuffled / salvage become vestigial; stable topic IDs become hard prerequisite (Session 5's stable-ID work promotes into pivot); Changes Ledger (Session 4) becomes ~80% subsumed (the operation list IS the ledger). **Director chose Option 2 (capture insight + restructure roadmap) at end of session.** ROADMAP gets new top-priority "🚨 ARCHITECTURAL PIVOT" section with multi-session plan: A (design + stable IDs) → B (deterministic applier + validation) → C (prompt rewrite) → D (wire it together + end-to-end test) → E (deprecate band-aids) → F (re-scope Sessions 4-6). 4-6 sessions across 2-3 weeks vs. continuing existing ~6-9-session patching. **Sessions 4-6 kept in ROADMAP for reference** with re-scope notes — Session 4 narrows to Changes Ledger UI on top of operations data; Session 5 stable-ID portion promoted into pivot, stability scoring portion remains as standalone polish; Session 6 mostly subsumed by pivot Session C's prompt rewrite. **Architectural pattern named (cross-tool, generalizable):** "AI as state-mutator (operations) vs. AI as state-rebuilder (full re-emission)." Re-emission scales O(state); operations scale O(change). For long-lived structured artifacts maintained across batches, default to operation-based output. Applies to any future PLOS workflow where AI maintains state across iterations. **Rule-16 lesson captured:** when adding any new mitigation/safety-net code, run the explicit zoom-out check *"is this making symptoms visible OR preventing the failure mode? If only making visible, what's the architectural change that would prevent the failure mode? Have we considered it?"* If the answer to the third is "no" or "we keep deferring it," surface to director rather than ship the next band-aid. **Decision pending for next session:** start Pivot Session A vs. continue with existing Sessions 4-6. Director may think on it overnight. **Second commit of session captured the insight + roadmap restructuring + KEYWORD_CLUSTERING_ACTIVE block + this row append.** **Resume point for next session:** clean `main` branch in sync with origin/main; ROADMAP "🚨 ARCHITECTURAL PIVOT" section is the new top of Phase 1; director's call on whether to start Pivot Session A (design + stable topic IDs) OR proceed with existing Sessions 4-6 plan OR start with the deferred blank-canvas visual verification first. |

## Historical chats (optional backfill by user)

If the user wants to add URLs of important past chats from their browser history:

```
| [Date] | [URL] | [Tool/System] | [Phase if known] | [Brief summary] |
```

---

## How to use this registry

### When Claude needs to point user to a past chat
Example: "You mentioned X. To unambiguously identify this data, please open the chat where we worked on [tool]. Based on CHAT_REGISTRY, the relevant chat is [URL]. In that chat, ask: '[precise question]'. Paste the answer back."

Selection process:
1. Match "Tool/System" and "Phase" to the topic of ambiguity
2. Pick the most recent matching chat
3. Give user the exact URL

### When user starts a new chat
Part of Group A — always uploaded. Doesn't need direct reference at start unless current work requires looking up past decisions.

### When a chat pivots mid-way
Add TWO rows for the same URL (one per scope). Claude requests URL capture again when the pivot happens (in practice URL is the same; purpose is logging scope change).

---

## End-of-chat URL confirmation (reminder)

Every chat ends with Claude asking: "Confirm the URL for this chat — paste the current address bar URL one more time so the registry entry is final."

---

## Archival strategy

If this file exceeds ~100 entries, oldest get moved to `CHAT_REGISTRY_ARCHIVE.md`. Active registry keeps most recent ~50 plus any marked structurally important (major architectural decisions).

Only triggered when actually needed.

---

END OF DOCUMENT
